And I will tell you the story of the man who had a leg infection. So that it might serve as an example and a help for your operation,
He was a young man of about thirty years of age, who had a pain in his leg, due to a growth that had risen up from within the body, that is, from inside, until it reached the flesh, and caused a large boil: but there was no external cause.
So when the time came with an error of the doctors, until it opened up and many fluids came out. And his treatment was postponed until his leg was wrapped up, and many holes were made in him: all of which discharged pus and body fluids.
Therefore many physicians had dealt with him for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands until I was called, and saw his wound, and the materials that flowed out of those orifices with a great course: also all his body was already dismembered, and his color was citrine.
So I inserted my hand into one of the orifices, and it came to the mouth.
Then I scrutinized all the orifices, and found them to pour out into one another on every side of the limb.
Then I dished it up, and followed one of the orifices until I detected part of the bone: and I found it to be corroded: which was already corroded, and blackened, and rotted, and pierced, until it penetrated all the way into the marrow.
Then I sharpened what I had detected, and prepared it from corrupt bone.
And I sheared off what was not in the bone except that corruption, which I could scrape off and sharpen. And I had already scraped it off.
Then I placed the wound with medical consolidates, spaced out in a long area. And this was not consolidated.
Then I inserted my hand again, and detected it on top of the first detection: and I found a continuous corruption with bone, and sharpened what was evident to me from that corruption as well.
Then I tried to restore it. And this was not restored.
Then I detected on top of the limb again, and did not cease to cut the bone in pieces, and try to restore it: and this was not restored until I cut from the bone a palm-length piece, and extracted it with its marrow.
Then I restored it with medical consolidates, and it healed quickly, and was cured: and this iteration in the operation, and cutting of itself, would not have been necessary but for the weakness of the nurse, and her lack of tolerance, and my fear over it dying: for it happened to him at all times from excessive bleeding during a syncopes.
He was therefore whole in his healing: and a new bone grew in the place of the old one, and good order was established in his body, and his strength returned; and he continued in his habits: and he did not cause him any harm at all in his walking.
But if the jaw is broken high up in the body already: then it should be closed by this means: that you take a piece of rope and tighten it at the end of the prominent bone; and you order someone to stretch it upwards: and you place another piece of rope, thicker than the first one, under the first. Then tie the wound over the flesh which is next to the bone; and extend the end of it, so that you pull the flesh down from below: and then you cover the place where you want to close it up, so that the flesh does not hurt when you cut it.
Place a piece of wood or a board under the bone from below: because when you do this, it does not hurt the corrupted flesh.
And it should be so that there is a little space over the corrupted flesh, so that the bone does not appear in its appearance; and it does not seem to feel any pain: and it pushes at its own will towards another closure.

Then close that part from the first where there is corruption until it continues in another part; and let the closure be at a little distance from the corruption in length as we have said.
That if the corruption is in the joint, then cut that joint which is corrupted, and close the bone where it continues from the other part.
But if the corruption is in the connection of two joints, then there is no sense of touch in it but only abrasion.
That if the corruption is in the palm of the hand or in the sole of the foot: then the matter in it is difficult to do much with. It is true that you should inquire how corruption appears to you. And cut off that part and clean it up in whatever way is possible for you, and with whatever skill you possess: when it does not give you a contrasting vein or nerve.
And know that many tools and saws are used to cut these bones depending on the position of the bones, and their preparation, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smoothness, and their rarity. Therefore it is necessary that you prepare the instrument suitable for any type of operation.

Regarding the care of abscesses, and the quality of the clisterization with medicines.
When an abscess happens to be in some fleshy member, and the abscess lasts long, until it collects pus: then it bursts, or pierces, and that which is in it comes out, and there remains a hollow place like a pit: and the skin that is over it is as thin cloth: and does not spread to the last degree of corruption, nor imprisons into the mouth, the nerves, or the ligaments: it deserves to be called a sinus: but does not carry the name of a fistula: nevertheless, if it prolongs its space, until it impresses corruption in some of these members, then it is called a fistula, or a sore.
And the cure is that you should strike off his whole skin like a sleeve; and especially when it has become thin, and made like a sheet of cloth; and believe that it will not stick to the place because of its corruption.
But if you hope that the skin will stick and that that corruption will not come to pass at the last consequence: and if there is a thickness of flesh on the skin, then cure him with clister; and consider towards the neck.
Then if it is large, and the pus that is discharged from it has a foul odor: then clisterize him with Egyptian medicine, which is vinegar, and oil, and myrrh, taking equal parts, mixed together in a vessel; and let them boil on the fire, until the medicine reddens; and let it come to a syrup.
Then take from it what you need; and dissolve it with water and honey, and clisterize it with him with the sin; and tighten the orifice of it, and let the medicine flow into it for two hours.
Then extract him with the expression; let him be for days until the sin is clean, and the smell is gone.
And when you clisterize it with water of ash, when this medicine is not present with you; and is, that you should take the ash of oak wood, or the ash of oak; and throw it on the water. Then boil it, and clisterize it with it, until you believe that the sin is now washed away.
That if the sick person does not tolerate Egyptian medicine or water of ash, then clisterize him with water and honey, to which has already been added some crushed myrrh. Or clisterize him with honey and wine mixed, for the property of honey is to clean and wash away; and the wine makes the sin adhere, especially when there is an abundance of stimulative and dry.
When you have done this sometimes and have trusted that the corruption of the sin has already been removed: then let him make him a clister, with what he does, to bring flesh into him.
And it is so that you may take from the plaster dyafinicon: and dissolve him with rose oil, and wine astringent: or make him a clister with certain medicines, and other ointments, whose properties I have written in the book of ointments.
That if the opening of the sinus is strict, in which the tube of the clister does not enter: then enlarge it a little with iron: or put in it the licorice that has been soaked in oil, in Egyptian ointment, or in basilico ointment, until it is enlarged.
And likewise if the opening is also wide, then join the lips together with a stitch: and let go out of it a quantity in which the clister is to be made without adding anything.
And likewise if the opening from which the pus runs is elevated towards the upper part: then dry him up in a lower place that is in him, so that the pus may run down from it: because when the pus is constricted in the depth of the sinus, it prohibits flesh to be generated in it.
That if it is not possible for you to dry the sinus all around below it according to what you want: then try, so that you prepare the member with preparation by which the pus runs out from it with ease according to what is prepared for you. Try so that nothing of the pus is left in it at all: and take medicines consolidatio that are placed over the mark, suited to what you want. And spread them on a linen cloth. And have there such a quantity of cloth that it may communicate with the whole sinus. Then cut with forceps on the direct opening of the sinus hole, a little larger opening of the sinus. Then spread on the other cloth with soft ointment according to the quantity of the hole: and put it in a distant position from the opening of the sinus, so that the outlet of the pus may be eased: and do not hold the cloth large, except after some days.
And yet he who is above the sinus opening, he whom you stir at all times so that he emerges from it with pus: and as you know, the infection that comes out of it is much or little, digested or undigested.
And when you consider this place of the sinus again, whether the master feels pain there or not; and if there is no pain there, and if there is a pus there, or not.
When your treatment therefore extends thus far, and you see the matter that comes out above the sinus opening; then know that the sinus is already attached, or approaching attachment: then therefore solve it in the morning, or on the third day; and when you have solved the wound, then change the cloth with another, and renew the unguent.
If however the pus comes out of the sinus after a long time, do not despair concerning its attachment, for its healing approaches, since there are people who delay the generation of flesh in their wounds, and there are those who bring it about in the opposite way.
But if the pus comes out of the sinus after many days, then know that the sinus is not attached.
But if the attachment of the sinus is delayed and its course is prolonged; then add to the drying up of medicines, that the doctors may make them dry in their substance, and in their power so as to be like the dyphinicon unguent, when added to it in excess of what is necessary from the oil.
And from this last, as regards its treatment, it is that you should take the dyphinicon unguent, and solve it with rose oil, and rub it on the old wound to the same extent as to its substance.
Then therefore bind it up with it, and use it.
And this same action is similar to that of the dye-finicon unguent when it is not present with you, and honey when you have decanted it until it thickens, and use it. Take myrrh and aloe and olive oil; let them be thoroughly mixed together and then put on honey while it is still hot above fire. Then bind a cloth over the wound and tie it tightly around the sinew: and with the honey that you have prepared, cover the wound until it thickens: and then apply the powder on the wound, and bind it again to the cloth, and tie it up.

Of the cure of the panaritus and the scratched nail, and the cutting of the finger added, and the sectioning.
Panaritus is an abscess that comes out under the nail of the thumb or foot, and perhaps also from the other fingers.

On the extraction of a vein from the leg.
This vein is generated in the legs in warm lands, such as Alizegi and the land of the Arabs, and in arid, hot lands, little tender, that is, in which grass does not grow, nor trees.
And perhaps it is generated in other parts of the body besides the legs.
And indeed its generation is from putrefaction which occurs under the skin, as it happens within the bodies of serpents and worms ascariuses, and worms generated between the skin and flesh.
And the sign of the beginning of this vein is, that it happens in the leg a hot inflammation. Then the place becomes blistered. Then the vein begins to issue out from the place of its blistering, as if it were a root of a plant, or an animal.
But when this extremitas of it appears, you shall then bind thereupon a fragment of lead whose weight is from a drachm to a claw-weight, up to two drachms and mark the same: and let go the lead suspended out of the leg.
Howsoever it shall go forth from it to the externals, bind it within the lead and mark it. Which if it should be prolonged for a long time, then cut a part of it, and bind the remainder. And do not cut it up into roots before it shall have gone forth all out. For if you should cut it, then it will contract itself and go into the flesh; and it makes happen a pustule, and decay in that place, and a bad wound.
So then it should be handled gently and slowly extracted until it has completely emerged from the last of its own, and nothing remains in the body: and from this very vein emerges in some people which is five palms long and ten. And I had already reached it because he had emerged from 20 palms.
But if you are injured at the time of your medical treatment: then insert a ray into that hole and pierce it with a long blade along with the body until all the contents have been completely discharged from it: and administer putrefaction to the site with medicines for several days. Then take care of him with the cure of wounds.
And this very vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears in the ankle of the foot, or in the foot itself: and many openings occur to it, and a branch emerges from every opening.
So then take care of it as we have said in division, and with the above-mentioned things that were preceded.
Regarding the section on worms born under the skin, and it is called the "bad trouble".
This "Illness" is called in some country "the bad trouble": for this often happens that worms emerge bare and a single one is born, which appears between skin and flesh.
And it was felt throughout the body when it rose and fell: and it was perceived by touch when it walked from one member to another, until it stopped wherever it stopped in the skin, and emerged.
And its origin is from the putrefaction of certain kinds of dung. As happen worms and snakes, that is, earthworms, and pinworms in the stomach.
And they fear its maliciousness. Because when he begins to move in the body and rises to a head, then perhaps it opens within him, and emerges, and destroys an eye: and this happens often.
So then if you are going to care for him and extract it, then that will not happen unless he walks or feels it himself.
Therefore, so that you keep what is above him, and what is below with strong constriction of the ligament. Then dry on top of him, and then extract him.
If it penetrates into the flesh, and not into his whole body: then place on the spot a cautery with fire until it dies.
And greater what is feared is corruption of him, which corrupts his eye, as we have said.
But if you see it has already reached the head near the eye, then tighten what is below with good tight constriction. Then dry on top of him, and then extract him.
And it is necessary that the sick one uses his own purification, with medicines dissolving bad putrid humors.
And he protects himself from foods that generate putrefaction.
§ On the section on disease of Nakir.
This disease is called in our land Nakir, and it is a pain that happens in some member, and then it changes from a member to another.
And indeed I have already seen him, according to what I tell you. I was called to a sick woman in some rooms. And she took her arm, and I saw swelling of the lung in the arm joint.
And after an hour had passed, I saw one swelling walk with a flame as if it were fire, rising faster than it can go: like silver in flight, when it runs from place to place.
So then the pain left that place, and was fixed in the shoulder.
Then he sat for an hour, and ran through the remaining body, until it reached another arm.
Then he told me that he was writhing all over his whole body, according to what I saw.
I am astounded at the swiftness with which he transfers his member from one part to another. And I too did not see this disease before, with my eyes, in such a way. However, I see many who suffer from the pain that one member causes another: and I do not see this one with my eyes, as I saw it in a woman.
And I do not think that this is, except that it is for this reason, because that woman was from those who are from dry bodies of stinking limbs: hence it appears to the sense that this swiftness is transferred.
And it is necessary so that it does not appear in this way with regard to those who are luscious and have humid bodies, of secret limbs.
When you then apply the cure to him, and the patient feels this pain: then if it appears to your eyes, as we have said, then lift him up quickly: and dry him out on top of him until he walks in that swiftness: and caustice the place.
If, however, you do not see this one with your eyes: then cure him by scrubbing the body, and with it what drives out the swiftness, and makes them red with foamy pills, and pills of bitter wormwood, and others like them.
Regarding the extraction of arrows.
Arrows differ according to their species, and according to the places in which they are embedded in the body.
However, there is a difference between them: for some have large tips, and some are sharp; and some are convexed, and some are concave. And of these some have three angles. And of these are the tongues. And of these are the stars.
However, those that fall into members according to the two ways. Or if members are from main concavities, like the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar to them. When therefore he falls upon any of these limbs, and the signs of death appear to you, which I shall tell you afterwards, then it is necessary that you should extract that arrow from him, for death will overtake him in that position. And when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not buried deep within the limb, then extract it, and be concerned for the wound.
For when the signs of injury to the brain appear, when an arrow falls into it, and pierces the bone, and comes out above the brain, there happen: for there is a violent headache, and blurring of vision, and dizziness, and reddening of the eyes, and swelling, and reddening of the tongue, and spasm, and confusion of thought, and loss of memory, and cholera. And perhaps blood comes out from the nose, or ears. And perhaps speech is severed, and the voice is destroyed. And there comes out of the wound's place a white, pulpy moisture. And there comes out of it similar to a meat broth.
But if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment, and extract the arrow if it has not come out.
The signs of an arrow that falls into the heart are: for it is near the left nipple: and feels as if fixed to a hard thing, not to a soft one. And perhaps the arrow has a movement similar to a pulse: and black blood runs from the limb. And follows it coldness of the limbs, and cold sweat, and fainting fit. So you know that death has certainly come.
And the sign of an arrow that wounds the lung is: blood spitting from the limb is frothy: and the veils that cover the neck, fall down, and change their color in front of the eyes. And he breathes out great, deep breaths: and seeks cold air.
If the arrow falls into the chest, which is within the breastplate: then it is close to the lower back: and it causes a great fever with severe pain, with sighing: and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
And if an arrow falls into the belly, then perhaps it has exited from a little indigestion from something eaten.
And if an arrow falls into the belly, and lodges there: it exits some stool from thebowels, or a piece of flesh, or an intestine which has already been torn. So there is no hope for its cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
If an arrow falls into the bladder, and it exits urine: and it proceeds from it something to the outside, and the pain is stronger over the sick one: then know that it is fatal.
The remaining limbs, such as the face, neck, mouth, spleens, ribs, hips, and legs, are saved according to multiple dispositions: when the arrow does not hit a blood vessel or nerve: and the arrow is not harmless.
And I tell you that I saw such arrows, which he used to indicate by way of example for your cure.
That is, because an arrow fell into the eye of a man's tear duct, at the root of his nose. So I extracted it from him on the other side, under the fat of his ear: and he was healed, and there was no harm to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from the Jew, which had fallen into his fat under his lower eyelid: and the arrow was now hidden, and I could not get it out unless I cut off part of his cheek, to which it was attached in its own wood: and it was a large arrow among the arrows of the Turks, with a soft iron, in which there were no bars.
So the Jew was healed, and there was no bad happen to his eye.
And I drew another bow from the throat of a Christian.
And it was an Arab bow, and that is where the ears are. Then I followed behind it with two arrows: and now she was submerged in his throat. So I went with care, until I had drawn her out: and the Christian was well.
And I drew out another arrow from a man who had fallen into his belly: and we thought that he should die therefrom.
After which I left him for thirty days, and there was nothing changed in him from his habits, then I followed behind the arrow: and I followed it up, and drew it out: and he was well, and no misfortune happened to him.
And I saw a man to whom the arrow had fallen on his back, and it was mending over him. After which it was after seven years, the arrow came out at the root of his hip.
And I saw a woman to whom the arrow had fallen into her belly, and it was mending over her, and the arrow remained within her: and there was nothing changed in her from her habits, and the woman did not find any harm in any of her natural actions.
And I saw another man to whom the arrow had fallen on his face, and it was mending over him, and remained, not finding much pain in it: and there were many such things like this.
And I drew out an arrow from the prince of the king, which had fallen into his nose, and was declining a little on the right side: and the arrow was hidden all together.
So I was called to his cure after the fall of the arrow for three days. Then I found the bow string very tight.
So I asked her with careful touch, and I did not feel it: but he himself felt the prick and pain under his right ear. I therefore hoped that it was that point at the end of the arrow.
I therefore prepared the plaster with which to draw out the force of attraction and digestion, confident within myself that if I should remove the place, a sign would appear to me of the arrow, so that I might cut over it: and this did not happen in the place suggesting that the arrow was lying in wait there.

Regarding the lancing of veins.
There are thirty veins from which blood is drawn.
Of these in the head there are sixteen: two pulse veins, which are behind the ears, called the two herbs; and two arteries, which appear in the two temples; and two veins which come from the two eyes, which are called the two lookers-about; and a vein which is prepared in the middle of the forehead; and a vein which is at the end of the nose. And two guide-veins, which are in the neck. And two veins which are in the upper lip of the mouth. And two veins which are in the lower lip. These are called the Algecirich veins. And two veins, which are under the tongue.
But the veins that are bled in the arms, there are five veins in every arm.
One of these ears is called the cephalic, and proceeds from the side of the skull; and it is named by the common name the vein of the head. And the Scaly. And there is a middle vein, which is composed of a basal and a cephalic branch; and it is named the common body vein. And the Basilica, and it is placed in the domestic side: and it is also called Titillicaris. And it is named by the people of many hands. And the tendon of the bicep, and it is placed on the edge of the wrist: and that one is in which bloodletting is done, and that one which appears above the thumb with a visible protrusion.
And the salvatory, and it is new which is between the ring and the little finger: and they are two branches.
And in the leg and in the foot there are three hands. One of them is that which is under the thumb on the side of the palm. And the second is the saphenous vein, and its place is at the heel from the domestic side. And the third is the nerve, and its place is at the heel on the side of the palm.
And in the other leg there are three hands like those.

On the utility of phlebotomy and on the precautions to be taken when performing it. The quality of phlebotomy and the complications that may arise from it, which you should consider how to correct.
First, then, of what you should be aware, that phlebotomy is administered not for the sake of health but to preserve it, and its persistence and caution from the advent of illness.
And so that phlebotomy is performed in one of three positions which a person lies in bed, namely the cephalic, the femoral, and the bazal. And so that phlebotomy is performed at the beginning of spring on a fasting person, in summer, and in autumn after a feast, when there are signs of fullness.
And so that phlebotomy is performed on the first or third day after having slept for three hours.
But phlebotomy which is administered to the sick does not have a determined hour; but when it elicits convenience and necessity towards it, at night, or by day, and at all times, and in all places.
And it is not appropriate that boys should be phlebotomized until they are fourteen years old. Nor should a pregnant woman be phlebotomized until the fourth month up to the seventh month. Nor should elderly people be phlebotomized who have already passed the age of sixty.
When anyone is to be phlebotomized, it is necessary that he should clean his intestines before phlebotomy with a laxative, if there is much waste retained in them: so that the blood does not attract venereal diseases from the intestines through the main veins.
Nor should a patient who is aching or nauseous from fasting be phlebotomized, nor should those who are drunk have it taken away from them until they have recovered from their intoxication. Nor should an invalid with hydrops be phlebotomized.
And let phlebotomy be repeated again after a fasting fever, and a lack of appetite, and a flow of urine, and an increase in sexual activity, and labor, and exercise, and vigils, and fasting, and all that dissolves virtue from the body or animal.
Then consider in subtlety of humors before that, if blood is thick with food and drink, and medicines: if possible is him that.
Then let the bath be introduced, if anything does not prohibit it: or he exercises a little exercise, in order to refine the blood.
And place the phlebotomy on his chest in his bosom, about the third day, as we have said: and be careful, that his chest should be drained of that blood that day from all animal bad accidents: such as anger, fear: and all bodily accidents, such as labor, punishment, excesses, and those like them.
And make these things available to him: because the custom of men is that they have always used aromatic substances, and their fragrance, and festivity, and such like, through the quantity of possibility.
Then let the phlebotomist sit on a table, that it be higher than the phlebotomy table: then he shall take his arm, and rub it with his own hand twice, or three times. Then let him tie the ligature with the cord, and roll it up once.
And let the constriction be strict, because constriction is unequal, or by excess in the constriction, then it prohibits the course of blood: or in softening, then also it prohibits the course of blood.
Then after the constriction, let the phlebotomist rub his hands together skin to skin, until the veins swell, and present themselves to the sense.
Then let the phlebotomist wipe the phlebotomy with a little oil, old, of his own proper.
Then let he put his right index finger of his left hand on the vein at the place where he intends to make a phlebotomy, little: so that the vein does not run away, and the piercing noise is not heard. For the veins are like a cord running away when making a phlebotomy: and those are full of blood: and when you put the phlebotomy on them, it is pinched under the phlebotomy, and deceives the phlebotomist, and does not open the vein: and if it opens it, then it is constricted: therefore, in all these things, let the phlebotomist rub himself, and be careful in these things.
Then deposit the phlebotomy. If then a new wound opens from one vein, then it is good. And if not, then repeat the other vein beneath that place a little, or above it with haste: if not the place swells up.
What if it swells up, or if the patient is feeble, then let him be discharged after one or two days: and do not tie a ligature tightly. For perhaps the swelling will be drawn in by the heat. And do not put him into a bath.
Then repeat the phlebotomy if he likes it.
What if the opening is small, or blood flows lightly: and be careful not to lose a quantity of blood more than you draw out: then repeat the phlebotomy in the same hole again, and add something to the procedure.
And do it quickly, before the place swells up: for the place will swell up in many people during a short time.
If then you see that he has already swelled up, then do not repeat the phlebotomy at all, for it does not excuse you with him for anything. And put something on the spot from a fat oil: for it will ease the course of blood. And this place is better than his own oil, and other oils better.
And likewise administer the fat oil in all your phlebotomies when you want to stop the course of blood: and they make it with myrrh when put on from one of these spots.
For blood is thickened and resolved when it is thin.
What if a great swelling occurs in the place where the phlebotomy has been made, for this often happens, especially when one has not had phlebotomy at that place before, or if a small opening has occurred, then bind it and put over the spot a sponge dipped in warm water and salt, and heat it slightly: and tie it up after an hour: for it is resolved.
It is necessary that you do this after the blood has come out from the wound itself with its own supply, or from another wound.
Which if it remains in the place for some days of redness or swelling does not harm that; and if there is a wound, put on it some aloe, or dissolved myrrh: or some juice of peppermint, that is, of calamus or similar to it.

The form of the Wind-afflicted when treated with fire.

[On the suspension of sanguine sugar].
Sanguine sugar should not be used in many cases, unless the limb is unable to hold a ventose because of its smallness, such as the lip, or the gum, or things like that. Or on a naked member devoid of flesh, such as a finger, or a nose, or things like that.
And the quality of their use is this: when you take them from sweet water where they are found, clean them from putrefaction.
Then let them be left overnight and the next day in sweet water until they are hungry, and there should not remain in their stomachs any of the drug. Then the body should be evacuated first with phlebotomy, and then with ventose. Then wash the limb with a nurse's hand until it turns red. Then place them on top of the limb.
When they are then filled and fall, and it is possible to suck the place with ventose, then it is better to use this method: if not, then wash the place with vinegar. Then with much water, and a rub, and squeeze out.
If the flow of blood is prolonged after the use of sanguine sugar and it remains sticky: then put a linen cloth in cold water, and place the limb upside down until the stickiness disappears.
If blood increases, then sprinkle the body with ground zegen, or gall, and things like that: until the blood stops flowing.
The middle parts of the vessels that have been cut should be placed on the site; and they should be left until the roots of the vessels have become attached to the site, since blood has been cut off.
And it is necessary that, if it is necessary, the blood sugar should be changed when it is possible, because it is not good to stay in one place.
But if the blood sugars are prohibited from suspension, then the site should be cleaned with recent blood. Or they should be placed in the places for a while until some of the blood has come out. Then they should be placed, because when they feel that they have some blood, they immediately become attached.
When you want them to fall off, sprinkle on them some crushed aloe, or salt, or ash: and they will fall off immediately.
